ARIE 1925-1926 [vol. 048]


APPENDIX A.


A. List of copper-plates examined during the year 1925-26.


ARIE/1925-1926/A/1925-26/1 (page 10)
Placement
Mr. M.S.Sarma of the Telugu Encyclopaedia office.
Dynasty
Eastern Chā-ḷukya.
King
…
Date
Śaka 982, Uttarāyaṇa-saṁkrānti.
Language
Sanskrit
Origin
Returned to the owner.
Edition
Epigraphia Indica.
Remarks
Records the gift of the village Avaraṅga in Kōlavarttana-vishaya as a bhōga to the god Jalēśvaradēva in the village. The date of the coronation of the king is given as Śaka 960.
ARIE/1925-1926/A/1925-26/2 (page 10)
Placement
Śrī L.N.Deb, Jubraj of Tek-kali.
Dynasty
Eastern Gaṅ-ga.
King
Mahārāja Indravarman
Date
Vijayarājya-samvatsara 87, Jyēshṭha, 10th day.
Language
Sanskrit in archaic characters
Origin
…
Edition
South-Indian Inscriptions.
Remarks
From a set of impressions received in the office from the Jubraj of Tekkali. Registers the grant of some land in the village Haribhaṭa, situated in the Kṛōshṭukavarttani, free of taxes, as dēvāgrahāra for worship and offerings and repairs in the temple of Rāmēśvara-Bhaṭṭāraka. The king bears the title Rajasiṁgha. The inscription was com-posed by Vinayachandra, son of Bhānu-chandra, and was engraved by Stapuṇōju.
ARIE/1925-1926/A/1925-26/3 (page 10)
Placement
Mr. Narayana Rao Deshpande, B.A., L.L.B., Pleader, Dhar-war, through Mr. N.Lak-shminarayana Rao of this office.
Dynasty
Western Chāḷukya.
King
Hiriya Hemmāḷirāya
Date
Śaka 100 [9], Ānanda (wrong), Chaitra, śu. 11, Monday.
Language
Kannaḍa in Nāgarī
Origin
Returned to the owner.
Edition
Epigraphia Indica.
Remarks
Seems to register a gift of land to the temple of Mūlasthāna Kalidēva at Vuṇḍāvar (?) by Bommeya-Nāyaka, a minister of the king who calls himself a great devotee of Bhūtanātha-dēva. Refers to the siege of the fortress Tōragallu during a great battle in which the king was victorious.
ARIE/1925-1926/A/1925-26/4 (page 10)
Placement
From the same gentleman through Mr. Lakshmi-narayana Rao.
Dynasty
Yādava
King
Siṅghaṇa
Date
Śaka 1173, Plavaṅga (wrong), Jyēshṭha, paurṇimā, Thursday, lunar eclipse.
Language
Sanskrit in Nāgarī
Origin
Returned to the owner.
Edition
Epigraphia Indica.
Remarks
Records the gift of shares in the village Niherüra to a number of brahmans by Malli-Śrēshṭhi, the son-in-law of Bīchirāya, the governor under the Yādava king.
ARIE/1925-1926/A/1925-26/5 (page 10)
Placement
The Tahsildar of Bezwada
Dynasty
Reḍḍi
King
Anavēma-Reḍḍi
Date
Śaka 1272, Bahudhānya, Māgha, ba. amāvāsyā, Sunday, solar eclipse.
Language
Telugu
Origin
Returned to the owner.
Edition
Epigraphia Indica.
Remarks
The king bears a number of birudas. Records the formation of a village called Vēmavaram to the east of Koṇḍapalli and its grant to Duggirāla Rāmaliṅgam and Mūlasthānam Sōmaliṅgam, who were experts in the intricacies of the Āgamas and Śaiva-śāstras. It also gives the names of the brahmans who performed worship in the temple and to whom some shares in the villages were allotted.
ARIE/1925-1926/A/1925-26/6 (page 10)
Placement
Mr. N.Seshagiri Rao, Settle-ment Revenue Inspector, Dharmavaram taluk, Ananta-pur, through Mr. A.Ranga-svami Sarasvati of this office.
Dynasty
Vijayanagara
King
Pratāpa-Dēvarāya
Date
Śaka 1339, Hēma(vi)ḷam-bi, Māgha, chaturdaśī, Śivarātri.
Language
Telugu
Origin
Returned to the owner.
Edition
South-Indian Inscriptions.
Remarks
Gift of the village Nāgireḍḍipalle, as sarva-mānya, to the brahman Dēvarasa, son of Bhāskaradēva, by the king.
ARIE/1925-1926/A/1925-26/7 (page 11)
Placement
From the Tahsildar, Dharma-varam taluk, Anantapur.
Dynasty
Vijayanagara
King
Śadāśivarāya-Mahārāya
Date
Śaka 1476, Ānanda, Āshāḍha, Utthāna-dvādaśi, Sunday.
Language
Sanskrit & Telugu in Nāgarī.
Origin
Returned to the owner.
Edition
South-Indian Inscriptions.
Remarks
Plates missing in the beginning. Registers the grant of Timmasamudram in Kanagāni-palli a village in the Gutti sub-division, to Appaḷāchārya, son of Tiruvēṅkaṭa Tātā-chārya and grandson of Penugoṇḍa Appayā-chārya. The grant was engraved by Śrīmallāchārya. The sign-manual of the king is engraved in Telugu as ‘Śrī-Virūpāksha.’

ARIE/1925-1926/A/1925-26/10 (page 11)

ARIE/1925-1926/A/1925-26/11 (page 11)
Placement
From Mr. D.Venkata-subba Rao, Reḍḍi of Gottur, same taluk.
Dynasty
…
King
…
Date
Śaka 1330, Sarvajit, Āśvija, śu. 7, Thursday.
Language
Telugu
Origin
Returned to the owner.
Edition
South-Indian Inscriptions.
Remarks
Records the gift of the right of paurōhityam in their community to a certain Rāmarasayya, son of Purushōttamayya and the grandson of Paugoṇḍa Naraharappa of the Kauṇḍinya-sagōtra and Āpastamba-sūtra, by a number of Ārya-Kshatriyas of the Muktarishi-vaṁśa, whose names are given. It also settles the fees that this priest was entitled to receive in their families on the several occasions.

ARIE/1925-1926/A/1925-26/13 (page 11)
Placement
From Mr. Gārachāvaḍi Pullayya, Clerk, Fund Office, Dharmavaram.
Dynasty
Do.
King
Prauḍhadēvarāya
Date
Śaka 1095, (wrong), Vija-[ya*], Māgha, ba. 12.
Language
Telugu
Origin
Returned to the owner.
Edition
South-Indian Inscriptions.
Remarks
Purports to register the grant of the tenure called dēśāyi-karaṇikam to a certain Tiru-mala-Mallarasu, by Mahāmaṇḍalēśvara Bhu-jabala Śōmadēvarāya-Mahārāya, an agent of the king, and gives a list of fields granted to him as remuneration in several villages.
ARIE/1925-1926/A/1925-26/14 (page 12)
Placement
From the same gentleman
Dynasty
Vijayanagara
King
Prauḍhadēvarāya, ruling at Vidyānagara-paṭṭaṇa.
Date
Śaka 1095, Śrīmukha, Āśvija, ba. 12.
Language
Kannaḍa & Telugu
Origin
Returned to the owner.
Edition
South-Indian Inscriptions.
Remarks
Purports to record a similar grant by the king, of the dēśāhi-karaṇika right over the vaḷitas of Tummala, Kanagānipalle, Pappūru and Yāḍiki, to Mallarasu, son of Nāgarasu and grandson of Vīrarasu of the Kauṇḍinya-gōtra. The grant is said to have been made for the merit of Virūpākshēśvara in the pre-sence of Kriyāśaktisvāmi. The villages of Vēlpu-maḍugu in the Tummala-sīma and Mālyavantam in the Pappūru-sīma were each renamed as Prauḍhadēvarāyapuram. The officer was given lands in several places as remuneration.
ARIE/1925-1926/A/1925-26/15 (page 12)
Placement
From a resident of Rāvula-cheruvu village, through the Tahsildar of Dharmavaram taluk.
Dynasty
Do.
King
Vijaya-Bukkarāya
Date
Śaka 1109, Jaya Āśvija, śu. 10.
Language
Telugu
Origin
Returned to the owner.
Edition
South-Indian Inscriptions.
Remarks
Purports to register the conferment of the reḍḍirikam right over Dharmavaram, in equal shares, on two families during the regime of Samprati Tipparājayya over Pen-namāgāṇi in Gutti-rājya. Also specifies several individuals as the holders of the vari-ous offices in the village, and the extent of the lands allotted to them. Mentions a Chikka-Oḍeya as having constructed the Dharmavaram tank and as having brought the idol of Chennakēśavasvāmi from Āne-gondi and consecrated it in the village.
ARIE/1925-1926/A/1925-26/16 (page 12)
Placement
From the Reḍḍi of Nasana-kota, same taluk, through Mr. A.Rangaswami Saras-vati.
Dynasty
Do.
King
Vīrapratāpa Bukkarāyadēva-Mahārāya, ruling from Vidyānagara.
Date
Śaka 1273, Ānanda, Vaiśākha, ba. 12.
Language
Telugu
Origin
Returned to the owner.
Edition
…
Remarks
The copper-plate bears on its top a solid image of two figures riding one behind the other on a single horse, the group being overshadowed by a serpent-hood. Purports to register the conferment of the gauḍirika right over the village Nasana in the Kanagānipalle-sīma, a sub-division of Pālēṭisthaḷa in Gutti-rājya, to Peda Chōḍama-Reḍḍi, and enumerates the lands granted to him.
ARIE/1925-1926/A/1925-26/17 (page 12)

From Pāḷegār Rāmappa, Toga-ragunta village, through the Tahsildar of Dharmavaram taluk.

Records the grant of the village Tūmicherla otherwise called Rāmachandrapuram, as sarvamānya to a number of brahmans at the request of Tōṭapa-Nāyaka, who was a subor-dinate of the king and was the son of Koṇḍama-Nāyaka and grandson of Tōṭapa. The village was divided into 40 shares.
ARIE/1925-1926/A/1925-26/18 (page 12)
Placement
From the District Judge of Vizagapatam.

…

Śaka 1665, Rudhirōdgāri, Bhādrapada, śu. 10, Wednesday.
Language
Telugu
Origin
…
Edition
…
Remarks
Records the grant as śrōtriyam of a village called Veṅkaṭāpuram formed out of the two hamlets of Pārummapēṭa and Bhaṭaripuram in the Mēraṅgitāluka, which were part of the estate of the donor Rājaśrī Śatrucharla Gaṅgarājugāru to Tirumala Veṅkaṭa-raṅgāchāryulu-Ayyavārlu, with the stipu-lation that the donee should pay Rs. 100 a year (as rent).
ARIE/1925-1926/A/1925-26/19 (page 13)
Placement
From the District Judge of Tinnevelly.
Dynasty
Madura Nāyaka.
King
Tirumalai-Nāyaka
Date
Achchuta (Akshaya ?), Vaikāśi 3.
Language
Tamil
Origin
…
Edition
…
Remarks
Purports to record the permission which the king granted, on the occasion of his visit to Bāvālippāḷaiyappaṭṭu, (when he was pleased with the reception accorded to him by the chief and four families from the north), to a certain Oṇḍippuli-Nāyaka, to found a village in the latter's name and to serve as a pāḷaiyakāraṉ of six villages under him. The surplus of revenue after deduct-ing 370 poṉ for himself as the pāḷaiyakāraṉ and 70 poṉ as nāṭṭāmai-mānibam, was directed to be sent to the kachchēri at Madurāpuri.
ARIE/1925-1926/A/1925-26/20 (page 13)
Placement
From the District Judge of Vizagapatam.
Dynasty
Nandāpūr
King
Mahārāja Vīra-Viśvambhara (II).
Date
Vibhava, Mithuna-saṅkrānti, Monday, (A.D. 1748, May 31st).
Language
Uriya
Origin
Returned to the owner.
Edition
…
Remarks
Read for this office by Mr. G.Ramadas Pantulu of Jeypore. Records a gift of 10 garsē of land (wet and dry) by the king to the Jaṅgam Pramabhi-pūjāri, the priest of the two temples of Mallikārjuna, for offerings to the deities during the three courses of worship of the day.

APPENDIX B.


Stone inscriptions copied in 1925--(continued from the last Annual Report).


ARIE/1925-1926/Stone inscriptions copied in 1925--(continued from the last Annual Report)/1925--/421 (page 14)
Placement
On the east wall of the central shrine in the Śishṭhēśvara temple at Tiruttalur, Cudda-lore taluk, South Arcot district.
Dynasty
Vijayanagara
King
Achyutadēva-Mahārāya
Date
....Śravaṇa....
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Built in at the beginning of each line. Seems to record a gift of land to the temple of Tavaneṟi-Āḷuḍai[yār] at Tiruttuṟaiyūr in Tiruvadich-chīmai of Vaḻudilambaṭṭu-śāvaḍi in Tirumuṉaippāḍi Kayappākka-nāḍu, a sub-divi-sion of Rājādhirāja-vaḷanāḍu, for providing for a kuḍai-yāḷ-mānyam to the servants of the temple.
ARIE/1925-1926/Stone inscriptions copied in 1925--(continued from the last Annual Report)/1925--/422 (page 14)
Placement
On the same wall
Dynasty
Do.
King
Mal[likārjuna*], son of Dēvaraya-Mahā-rāya, ‘who instituted the elephant hunt’.
Date
Śaka 1409, Viśvā-[va*]su, Siṁha, śu. tritīyā, Fri-day ....
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Built in at the right end. Records a royal charter given to the kaikkōḷas of the kingdom, entitling them to the honour of taṇḍu (palanquin) and conch-shell (bugle), in response to their representation to Aṟamaḷatta-Nayiṉār at Kāñchīpuram.
ARIE/1925-1926/Stone inscriptions copied in 1925--(continued from the last Annual Report)/1925--/423 (page 14)
Placement

Dynasty

Rājakēsarivarmaṉ alias Tribhuvana-chakravartin Kulōttuṅga-Chōḷadēva.
Date
10th year
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Begins with the introduction pUmEvivaLara, etc. Records the a gift of cows by two brothers for burning a lamp in the temple at Tiruttuṟaiyūr in Tirumuṉaippāḍi, a sub-division of Rājarāja-vaḷanāḍu.

ARIE/1925-1926/Stone inscriptions copied in 1925--(continued from the last Annual Report)/1925--/428 (page 14)
Placement
Do.
Dynasty
Do.
King
Narasiṅgadēva-Mahārāya
Date
Vikṛiti, Aṟpaśi 12.
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Records the remission of certain taxes due on some newly formed villages, granted by the king through his avasa-ram Annamaraśar in favour of the temples of Tavaneṟi-Āḷuḍaiya-Nāyaṉār, Vīmīśuram-Uḍaiyār and Irāśūr-Uḍai-yār and to the other temples of the village-group (paṟṟu) for the maintenance of the monthly festivals in them in the asterism Makhā and for renovating the several adjuncts of the temples, which had been in a bad state for several years.

States that he was crowned on the date of the inscription, when he granted the villages Kōkallu other-wise called Sabbāmbikāpuram for the merit of his mother, the villages Giñjipāḍu, Challagara and Tāḍuvāya for his father's merit under the name Bhīmavaram, Ammala-pūnḍi under the name Chōḍavaram for the merit of his elder brother Kōṭa-Chōḍarāju and the villages Sattana-palle, Uppalapāḍu, Chintapalli, O1ṁkadoni and Kuṁṭi-maddi for his own merit.
